Compartment Transitions:\\n- S → E: Susceptible individuals become exposed through contact with infectives.        +configure(level: str = \"INFO\") logging.Logger\n    }\n\n    CLI ..> Config : uses\n    Config ..> SEIRDParams : creates\n    Config ..> SEIRDState : creates\n    SEIRDSimulator o-- SEIRDModel : has\n    SEIRDSimulator ..> SEIRDParams : uses\n    SEIRDModel ..> SEIRDState : reads/writes\n    SEIRDModel ..> SEIRDStepResult : returns\n    CLI ..> JsonlWriter : outputs\n    CLI ..> Log : configures\n```\n\n### Key functions (math)\n`SEIRDModel.step()` implements exactly:\n- `new_exposed = (β * S_old * I_old / N) * dt` then `min(new_exposed, S_old)`\n- `new_infective = (E_old / incubation_period) * dt` then `min(new_infective, E_old)`\n- `new_deceased = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (mortality/100) * dt`\n- `new_recovered = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (1 - mortality/100) * dt`\n- Apply compartment updates as specified.\n\n## Program call flow\n\n(See also: `docs/system_design-sequence-diagram.mermaid`)\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant U as User/Shell\n    participant CLI as CLI(main)\n    participant CFG as Config\n    participant LOG as Log\n    participant SIM as SEIRDSimulator\n    participant MOD as SEIRDModel\n    participant OUT as If you want a DEVS or event-sim version, specify expected event schema and scheduling.\n"

A plain loop is simpler, deterministic, and easier to teach.\n- `simpy` / `xdevs` remain optional/future extensions (event-based or DEVS modeling), not required for this spec.\n\n### Libraries\n- **argparse**: CLI parsing (required).\n- **json + sys**: JSONL-only stdout; logs to stderr.\n- **logging**: debug/progress on stderr.\n\n### Edge-case handling\n- Validate configuration:\n  - `total_population >= 0`, `initial_infective >= 0`, and `initial_infective <= total_population`.\n  - `dt > 0`, `simulation_time >= 0`.\n  - `incubation_period > 0`, `infectivity_period > 0`.\n  - `0 <= mortality <= 100`.\n- For `N == 0`: no transmission; all compartments remain 0; still output final JSON.\n- Numerical stability:\n  - Clamp flows using `min(flow, compartment)` as required.\n  - Clamp compartments to `>= 0.0` after each step (to avoid small negative drift).\n  - Optional (documented) conservation check `abs((S+E+I+R+D) - N) < eps` logged to stderr.\n\n## File list\n\n- It is for teaching demonstration purpose to show the ODEs. \\nThe population is divided into five compartments:\\n- S (Susceptible): Individuals who can be infected.\\n- E (Exposed): Individuals who are infected but not yet infectious. \\n- I (Infective): Individuals who are infected and can transmit the disease. \\n- R (Recovered): Individuals who have recovered and are immune. \\n- D (Deceased): Individuals who have died from the disease. \\n\\n2. Model Characteristics:\\n- Homogeneous Mixing: All individuals have equal contact probability\\n- Closed Population: No births, deaths (other than disease), or migration\\n- Discrete-Time: State updates occur at fixed time intervals (dt)\\n\\n3. Compartment Transitions:\\n- S → E: Susceptible individuals become exposed through contact with infectives. Rate: β * S * I / N per day (where β is transmission rate, N is total population)\\n- E → I: Exposed individuals become infectious after incubation period. Rate: E / incubation_period per day\\n- I → R: Infective individuals recover. Rate: I / infectivity_period * (1 - mortality/100) per day\\n- I → D: Infective individuals die. It is for teaching demonstration purpose to show the ODEs. \\nThe population is divided into five compartments:\\n- S (Susceptible): Individuals who can be infected.\\n- E (Exposed): Individuals who are infected but not yet infectious. \\n- I (Infective): Individuals who are infected and can transmit the disease. \\n- R (Recovered): Individuals who have recovered and are immune. \\n- D (Deceased): Individuals who have died from the disease. \\n\\n2. Model Characteristics:\\n- Homogeneous Mixing: All individuals have equal contact probability\\n- Closed Population: No births, deaths (other than disease), or migration\\n- Discrete-Time: State updates occur at fixed time intervals (dt)\\n\\n3. Compartment Transitions:\\n- S → E: Susceptible individuals become exposed through contact with infectives. Rate: β * S * I / N per day (where β is transmission rate, N is total population)\\n- E → I: Exposed individuals become infectious after incubation period. Rate: E / incubation_period per day\\n- I → R: Infective individuals recover. Rate: I / infectivity_period * (1 - mortality/100) per day\\n- I → D: Infective individuals die. Rate: I / infectivity_period * (mortality/100) per day\\n\\n4. Language & Project Info\n\n### 1.1 Target Language / Environment\n- **Target Language:** Python **3.10+**\n- **Standard Libraries / Allowed Libraries:** `argparse`, `sys`, `json`, `logging`, `collections`, `random`, `simpy`, `xdevs`\n  - Note: Even if `simpy` / `xdevs` are not strictly required for the discrete-time ODE-style update loop, they are explicitly permitted and must remain compatible with the project.\n\n### 1.2 Project Name\n- **Project name (snake_case):** `seird_cli_simulator`\n\n### 1.3 Entry Point / Project Constraint\n- The deliverable **MUST** be a Python project.\n- The entry point **MUST** be named: **`run.py`**\n\n### 1.4 Restated Requirements (Do Not Lose Details)\n**General implementation requirements**\n1. Language & Environment:\n   - Python 3.10+\n   - Standard Libraries: `argparse`, `sys`, `json`, `logging`, `collections`, `random`, `simpy`, `xdevs`.\n2. Input Interface:\n   - **CLI arguments:** MUST use `argparse` to handle configuration parameters.\n   - **Data stream:** If dynamic input is required, read from `sys.stdin` line-by-line.\n   - For this scenario: **No stdin input is required**.\n3. Output Interface:\n   - **Stream 1 (stdout):** Final State\n     - MUST print **ONLY JSONL objects** containing the required events.\n     - MUST follow the schema described below.\n     - Example: `print(json.dumps({...}))`\n   - **Stream 2 (stderr):** Debug/log\n     - Any other information (debug, progress, warnings) MUST go to **`sys.stderr`**.\n4. Time Format & Units:\n   - Output JSONL `time` values MUST be **floats** representing **absolute simulation time starting at `0.0`**.\n   - Precision: Keep **at least 2 decimal places**.\n\n**Scenario: SEIRD compartmental model**\n- Objective: simulate infectious disease spread in a **closed population** using the **SEIRD** compartmental model, for teaching demonstration to show the ODE-style updates.\n- Compartments:\n  - **S** Susceptible\n  - **E** Exposed (infected, not yet infectious)\n  - **I** Infective (infectious)\n  - **R** Recovered (immune)\n  - **D** Deceased\n- Characteristics:\n  - Homogeneous mixing\n  - Closed population: no births, no migration; only disease deaths\n  - Discrete-time: updates at fixed time interval `dt`\n- Transitions / rates per day:\n  - S → E: `β * S * I / N`\n  - E → I: `E / incubation_period`\n  - I → R: `I / infectivity_period * (1 - mortality/100)`\n  - I → D: `I / infectivity_period * (mortality/100)`\n- Calculation details (per time step):\n  - `new_exposed = (β * S_old * I_old / N) * dt`; `new_exposed = min(new_exposed, S_old)`; `S_new = S_old - new_exposed`\n  - `new_infective = (E_old / incubation_period) * dt`; `new_infective = min(new_infective, E_old)`; `E_new = E_old + new_exposed - new_infective`\n  - `new_deceased = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (mortality/100) * dt`\n  - `new_recovered = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (1 - mortality/100) * dt`\n  - `I_new = I_old + new_infective - new_deceased - new_recovered`\n  - `R_new = R_old + new_recovered`\n  - `D_new = D_old + new_deceased`\n- Constraints:\n  - Time unit: **1.0 = 1 day**\n  - Population conservation: `S + E + I + R + D = total_population` (within floating-point precision)\n  - Initial state:\n    - `S = N - I_0`, `E = 0`, `I = I_0`, `R = 0`, `D = 0`\n  - System starts immediately at time `0.0`\n\n**CLI args**\n- `--test_name` (str) **required**\n- `--mortality` (float, 0–100), default **10.0**\n- `--infectivity_period` (float), default **14.0**\n- `--dt` (float), default **0.1**\n- `--incubation_period` (float), default **5.0**\n- `--total_population` (int, integer >= 0), default **1000**\n- `--initial_infective` (int), default **10**\n- `--transmission_rate` (float, β), default **2.5**\n- `--simulation_time` (float), default **10.0**\n\n**stdout schema (JSONL)**\n- Output at the end of simulation (and other JSON objects are also allowed), but stdout MUST be JSONL-only.\n- At least the final state object:\n```json\n{\n  \"time\": <float>,\n  \"susceptible\": <float>,\n  \"exposed\": <float>,\n  \"infective\": <float>,\n  \"recovered\": <float>,\n  \"deceased\": <float>\n}\n```\n- Values must be floats with **>= 2 decimals**.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Product Definition (IMPORTANT)\n\n### 2.1 Product Goals (3 orthogonal goals)\n1. **Correctness & Reproducibility:** Implement the SEIRD discrete-time update exactly as specified, maintaining population conservation within floating-point tolerance and producing deterministic results for the same parameters.\n2. **CLI-first Teaching Utility:** Provide a simple, inspectable CLI that makes it easy to run parameterized SEIRD simulations for classroom/demo usage and automated tests.\n3. **Strict I/O Contracts for Integration:** Ensure stdout emits **JSONL-only** objects (no stray prints), and all logs/debug go to stderr, enabling safe piping and automated evaluation.\n\n### 2.2 User Stories (3–5)\n1. **As a teacher**, I want to run a SEIRD simulation with different parameters (β, dt, incubation/infectivity, mortality) so that I can demonstrate how epidemic curves change.\n2. **As a student**, I want a single JSON output with final compartment sizes so that I can verify my understanding and compare results.\n3. **As an auto-grader author**, I want strict JSONL-only stdout so that I can parse outputs reliably in scripts.\n4. **As a developer**, I want logs on stderr so that I can troubleshoot without corrupting JSONL output.\n5. **As a researcher prototyper**, I want a lightweight baseline SEIRD simulator so that I can extend it later (e.g., add intermediate outputs, alternative integrators) while keeping the same core update rules.\n\n### 2.3 Competitive Analysis (5–7 products)\n> Focus: tools that users might choose instead of a simple CLI SEIRD simulator for teaching or quick experiments.\n\n1. **Covasim (agent-based COVID simulator)**\n   - Pros: High realism; interventions; rich outputs.\n   - Cons: Heavier setup; overkill for teaching ODE-style compartment updates; not a minimal CLI JSONL tool.\n\n2. **EpiModel (R package)**\n   - Pros: Mature epidemiological modeling; flexible network/compartmental frameworks.\n   - Cons: Requires R; learning curve; integration with Python-only pipelines not direct.\n\n3. **PyRoss (Python epidemiology modeling library)**\n   - Pros: Designed for compartmental models; richer math tooling.\n   - Cons: Library-centric rather than minimal CLI; may introduce complexity for basic demonstrations.\n\n4. **AnyLogic (commercial simulation platform)**\n   - Pros: Visual modeling; combines system dynamics and agent-based.\n   - Cons: Commercial licensing; less suitable for lightweight CLI + JSONL-only stdout requirements.\n\n5. **GLEAMviz (epidemic modeling platform)**\n   - Pros: Strong for spatial/mobility-based models.\n   - Cons: Not aligned with “closed population, homogeneous mixing, discrete dt” teaching baseline.\n\n6. **NetLogo epidemic models (e.g., Virus model)**\n   - Pros: Great for interactive teaching and visualization.\n   - Cons: Agent-based and GUI-first; not a strict CLI JSONL interface; different assumptions.\n\n7. **Generic SEIR notebooks / web demos (e.g., Jupyter-based SEIR demos)**\n   - Pros: Easy to visualize and modify interactively.\n   - Cons: Not standardized CLI; stdout mixing/logging; less suitable for automated grading.\n\n### 2.4 Competitive Quadrant Chart (Mermaid)\nAxes:\n- X-axis: **Ease of Integration (CLI/automation + strict machine-readable outputs)**\n- Y-axis: **Model Fidelity / Feature Richness**\n\n```mermaid\nquadrantChart\n  title \"SEIRD CLI Simulator vs Alternatives\"\n  x-axis \"Low Integration Ease\" --> \"High Integration Ease\"\n  y-axis \"Low Fidelity/Features\" --> \"High Fidelity/Features\"\n  quadrant-1 \"Feature-rich + easy to integrate\"\n  quadrant-2 \"Feature-rich but heavier\"\n  quadrant-3 \"Basic and harder to integrate\"\n  quadrant-4 \"Basic + easy to integrate\"\n  \"AnyLogic\": [0.30, 0.85]\n  \"GLEAMviz\": [0.35, 0.80]\n  \"Covasim\": [0.45, 0.90]\n  \"EpiModel\": [0.40, 0.75]\n  \"NetLogo\": [0.55, 0.65]\n  \"SEIR Jupyter demos\": [0.60, 0.50]\n  \"Our Target Product (seird_cli_simulator)\": [0.90, 0.45]\n```\n\n---\n\n## 3. Technical Specifications\n\n### 3.1 Requirements Analysis (Comprehensive)\n\n#### 3.1.1 Simulation Core\n- The simulation MUST implement a **discrete-time update loop** from `time=0.0` to `time=simulation_time`, stepping by `dt`.\n- State variables MUST be stored as floats: `S`, `E`, `I`, `R`, `D`.\n- The update MUST use the **exact equations and min-capping rules** provided:\n  - `new_exposed = (β * S_old * I_old / N) * dt`, then `min(new_exposed, S_old)`\n  - `new_infective = (E_old / incubation_period) * dt`, then `min(new_infective, E_old)`\n  - `new_deceased = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (mortality/100) * dt`\n  - `new_recovered = (I_old / infectivity_period) * (1 - mortality/100) * dt`\n  - Updates must occur using `_old` values consistently per step.\n- The simulator MUST preserve population conservation within floating-point tolerance.\n\n#### 3.1.2 Configuration / CLI\n- The program MUST use `argparse` and accept the following named arguments:\n  - `--test_name` (str) required\n  - `--mortality` (float, %), default 10.0\n  - `--infectivity_period` (float), default 14.0\n  - `--dt` (float), default 0.1\n  - `--incubation_period` (float), default 5.0\n  - `--total_population` (int >= 0), default 1000\n  - `--initial_infective` (int), default 10\n  - `--transmission_rate` (float β), default 2.5\n  - `--simulation_time` (float), default 10.0\n- No stdin is required for the baseline scenario. If extended later, dynamic input MUST be read from `sys.stdin` line-by-line.\n\n#### 3.1.3 Output Contract (Strict)\n- stdout MUST contain **only JSONL** objects.\n- At minimum, the final JSON object MUST be printed at the end of simulation with fields:\n  - `time`, `susceptible`, `exposed`, `infective`, `recovered`, `deceased`\n- All numeric outputs MUST be floats with at least **2 decimal places**.\n- Any logs, warnings, progress updates MUST be written to **stderr**.\n\n#### 3.1.4 Logging & Observability\n- Use `logging` configured to write to stderr.\n- The code SHOULD avoid printing anything to stdout except JSONL.\n\n#### 3.1.5 Robustness / Validation\n- Input validation MUST guard against invalid configurations that would break equations (e.g., division by zero):\n  - `total_population` must be >= 0\n  - `initial_infective` should be >= 0 and ideally <= total_population\n  - `dt` > 0\n  - `incubation_period` > 0\n  - `infectivity_period` > 0\n  - `mortality` in [0, 100]\n- If invalid, program SHOULD exit non-zero and write an actionable message to stderr.\n\n### 3.2 Requirements Pool (P0/P1/P2)\n\n#### P0 (Must-have)\n1. `run.py` as entry point.\n2. Python 3.10+ compatible.\n3. CLI implemented with `argparse`, including all required arguments and defaults.\n4. Implement SEIRD discrete-time update exactly as specified, including min-caps.\n5. Initial state MUST be `S=N-I0, E=0, I=I0, R=0, D=0` at time `0.0`.\n6. Simulation time tracking MUST output absolute `time` starting at `0.0` and ending at final simulation time as float.\n7. stdout MUST be JSONL-only; at least one final JSON object with required schema.\n8. All non-JSON output MUST go to stderr.\n9. Output floats must have **>= 2 decimals**.\n\n#### P1 (Should-have)\n1. Optional intermediate JSONL outputs (e.g., per step or per day) controlled via an additional CLI flag (would need spec approval).\n2. Population conservation check each step (tolerance-based) and warning to stderr if drift exceeds threshold.\n3. Deterministic rounding strategy for output formatting (e.g., `round(x, 2)` or formatted to 2 decimals but stored as float).\n\n#### P2 (Nice-to-have)\n1. Export of full time series to JSONL (one object per timestep) for plotting.\n2. Support for seeded randomness for future stochastic extensions (keeping current model deterministic).\n3. Optional integration scaffolding for `simpy` or `xdevs` without changing baseline deterministic behavior.\n\n### 3.3 UI Design Draft (Basic layout and functionality)\n\n#### 3.3.1 CLI UX\n- Invocation pattern:\n  - `python run.py --test_name <name> [--mortality ...] [--dt ...] ...`\n- Help output must be provided by argparse `--help`.\n\n.
